<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">System or group of people governing an organized community, often a state</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For the executive of parliamentary systems referred to as the government, see <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive (government)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Government_(disambiguation)" title="Government (disambiguation)">Government (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#b9b9b9; color:#b9b9b9;">    </span> No government </span></span></td><td><span style="font-size:small;"></span></td></tr> <tr style="vertical-align:top;"><td><span style="font-size:small;"></span></td><td><span style="font-size:small;"></span></td></tr> <tr style="vertical-align:top;"><td><span style="font-size:small;"></span></td><td><span style="font-size:small;"></span></td></tr> </tbody></table> </td></tr></tbody></table> <sup>1</sup> This map was compiled according to the Wikipedia <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_system_of_government" title="List of countries by system of government">list of countries by system of government</a></i>. <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_sidebar" title="Template:Politics sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_sidebar" title="Template talk:Politics sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>A <b>government</b> is the system or group of people governing an organized community, generally a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a>.
</p><p>In the case of its broad associative definition, government normally consists of <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a>. Government is a means by which organizational policies are enforced, as well as a mechanism for determining policy. In many countries, the government has a kind of <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a>, a statement of its governing principles and philosophy.
</p><p>While all types of organizations have <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">governance</a>, the term <i>government</i> is often used more specifically to refer to the approximately 200 <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">independent national governments</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governmental_organization" title="Governmental organization">subsidiary organizations</a>.
</p><p>Historically prevalent forms of government include <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timocracy" title="Timocracy">timocracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">theocracy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyranny</a>. These forms are not always mutually exclusive, and <a href="/wiki/Mixed_government" title="Mixed government">mixed governments</a> are common. The main aspect of any philosophy of government is how political power is obtained, with the two main forms being <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">electoral contest</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hereditary_succession" title="Hereditary succession">hereditary succession</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions_and_etymology">Definitions and etymology</span></h2>
<p>A government is the <a href="/wiki/System" title="System">system</a> to <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">govern</a> a <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> or community. The <i><a href="/wiki/Columbia_Encyclopedia" title="Columbia Encyclopedia">Columbia Encyclopedia</a></i> defines government as "a system of social control under which the right to make laws, and the right to enforce them, is vested in a particular group in society".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> While all types of organizations have <a href="/wiki/Governance" title="Governance">governance</a>, the word <i>government</i> is often used more specifically to refer to the approximately 200 <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">independent national governments</a> on Earth, as well as their subsidiary organizations, such as <a href="/wiki/State_government" title="State government">state and provincial governments</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local governments</a>.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmelserBaltes2001[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_2-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmelserBaltes2001[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-2'>[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>The word <i>government</i> derives from the Greek verb <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">κυβερνάω</span></span> [<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn">kubernáo</i></span>] meaning <i>to steer</i> with a <a href="/wiki/Gubernaculum_(classical)" title="Gubernaculum (classical)">gubernaculum</a> (rudder), the metaphorical sense being attested in the literature of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ship_of_State" title="Ship of State">Ship of State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrock201353–62_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrock201353–62-3">[3]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>, "government" sometimes refers to what's also known as a "<a href="/wiki/Ministry_(collective_executive)" title="Ministry (collective executive)">ministry</a>" or an "<a href="/wiki/Administration_(government)" title="Administration (government)">administration</a>", i.e., the policies and government officials of a particular executive or governing <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition</a>. Finally, <i>government</i> is also sometimes used in English as a <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">synonym</a> for rule or governance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Political_history_of_the_world" title="Political history of the world">Political history of the world</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_philosophy" title="Political philosophy">Political philosophy</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earliest_governments">Earliest governments</span></h3>
<p>The moment and place that the phenomenon of human government developed is lost in time; however, history does record the formations of early governments. About 5,000 years ago, the first small city-states appeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245-5">[5]</a></sup> By the third to second millenniums BC, some of these had developed into larger governed areas: <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley_civilization" title="Indus Valley civilization">Indus Valley civilization</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Neolithic_cultures_of_China" title="List of Neolithic cultures of China">Yellow River civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2004294_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2004294-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>The development of agriculture and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_control" title="Water control">water control</a> projects were a catalyst for the development of governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica2010_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2010-7">[7]</a></sup> On occasion a chief of a tribe was elected by various rituals or tests of strength to govern his tribe, sometimes with a group of elder tribesmen as a council. The human ability to precisely communicate abstract, learned information allowed humans to become ever more effective at agriculture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2004146–147_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2004146–147-8">[8]</a></sup> and that allowed for ever increasing population densities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Christian_(historian)" title="David Christian (historian)">David Christian</a> explains how this resulted in states with laws and governments.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>As farming populations gathered in larger and denser communities, interactions between different groups increased and the social pressure rose until, in a striking parallel with star formation, new structures suddenly appeared, together with a new level of complexity. Like stars, cities and states reorganize and energize the smaller objects within their gravitational field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2004245-5">[5]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_governments">Modern governments</span></h3>
<p>Starting at the end of the 17th century, the prevalence of republican forms of government grew. The <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> in England, the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> contributed to the growth of representative forms of government. The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> was the first large country to have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">Communist</a> government.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmelserBaltes2001[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_2-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmelserBaltes2001[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-2'>[2]</a></sup> Since the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a> has become an even more prevalent form of government.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuperKuper2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_9-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuperKuper2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-9'>[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the nineteenth and twentieth century, there was a significant increase in the size and scale of government at the national level.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaider-Markel2014[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_10-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaider-Markel2014[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-10'>[10]</a></sup> This included the regulation of corporations and the development of the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKuperKuper2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_9-1'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKuperKuper2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-9'>[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_science">Political science</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">Political science</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span></h3>
<p>In political science, it has long been a goal to create a typology or taxonomy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polities" title="Polities">polities</a>, as typologies of political systems are not obvious.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewellen2003[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_11-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewellen2003[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_July_2022]]&lt;sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;"&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(July_2022)"&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-11'>[11]</a></sup> It is especially important in the <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> fields of <a href="/wiki/Comparative_politics" title="Comparative politics">comparative politics</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>. Like all categories discerned within forms of government, the boundaries of government classifications are either fluid or ill-defined.
</p><p>Superficially, all governments have an official or ideal form. The United States is a constitutional republic, while the former Soviet Union was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_republic" title="Socialist republic">socialist republic</a>. However self-identification is not objective, and as Kopstein and Lichbach argue, defining regimes can be tricky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKopsteinLichbach20054_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKopsteinLichbach20054-12">[12]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> argued that "the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> is neither Holy, nor Roman, nor an Empire".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenna2015_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenna2015-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Identifying a form of government is also difficult because many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_systems" title="Political systems">political systems</a> originate as socio-economic movements and are then carried into governments by parties naming themselves after those movements; all with competing political-ideologies. Experience with those movements in power, and the strong ties they may have to particular forms of government, can cause them to be considered as forms of government in themselves.
</p><p>Other complications include general non-consensus or deliberate "<a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">distortion or bias</a>" of reasonable technical definitions to political ideologies and associated forms of governing, due to the nature of politics in the modern era. For example: The meaning of "conservatism" in the United States has little in common with the way the word's definition is used elsewhere. As Ribuffo notes, "what Americans now call conservatism much of the world calls liberalism or <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a>"; a "conservative" in Finland would be labeled a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a>" in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERibuffo20112–6quote_on_p._6_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERibuffo20112–6quote_on_p._6-14">[14]</a></sup> Since the 1950s conservatism in the United States has been chiefly associated with the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="History of the Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>. However, during the era of <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">segregation</a> many <a href="/wiki/Southern_Democrats" title="Southern Democrats">Southern Democrats</a> were conservatives, and they played a key role in the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_coalition" title="Conservative coalition">conservative coalition</a> that controlled Congress from 1937 to 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrederickson200012_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrederickson200012-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[a]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social-political_ambiguity">Social-political ambiguity</span></h3>
<p>Opinions vary by individuals concerning the types and properties of governments that exist. "Shades of gray" are commonplace in any government and its corresponding classification. Even the most liberal democracies limit rival political activity to one extent or another while the most tyrannical dictatorships must organize a broad base of support thereby creating difficulties for "<a href="/wiki/Pigeonholing" title="Pigeonholing">pigeonholing</a>" governments into narrow categories. Examples include the claims of the <a href="/wiki/Plutocracy#United_States" title="Plutocracy">United States as being a plutocracy</a> rather than a democracy since some American voters believe elections are being manipulated by wealthy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Super_PACs" title="Super PACs">Super PACs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreeland2012_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreeland2012-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p>

</tr><tr><th class="sidebar-heading">
<a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">Administrative division</a></th></tr></tbody></table></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="background:#efefef;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Basic_forms_of_government" title="Template:Basic forms of government"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Basic_forms_of_government" title="Template talk:Basic forms of government"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Basic_forms_of_government&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_forms_of_government" title="List of forms of government">List of forms of government</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Plato%27s_five_regimes" title="Plato's five regimes">Plato's five regimes</a></div>
<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Republic_(Plato)" title="Republic (Plato)">Republic</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a> discusses five types of regimes: <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timocracy" title="Timocracy">timocracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>, democracy, and <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyranny</a>. These five regimes progressively degenerate starting with aristocracy at the top and tyranny at the bottom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrill2016_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrill2016-18">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his <i><a href="/wiki/Politics_(Aristotle)" title="Politics (Aristotle)">Politics</a></i>, Aristotle elaborates on Plato's five regimes discussing them in relation to the government of one, of the few, and of the many.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> From this follows the classification of forms of government according to which people have the authority to rule: either one person (an <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocracy</a>, such as monarchy), a select group of people (an aristocracy), or the people as a whole (a democracy, such as a republic).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a> stated on their classification:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The difference of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth" title="Commonwealth">Commonwealths</a> consisteth in the difference of the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign" title="Sovereign">sovereign</a>, or the person representative of all and every one of the multitude. And because the sovereignty is either in one man, or in an assembly of more than one; and into that assembly either every man hath right to enter, or not every one, but certain men distinguished from the rest; it is manifest there can be but three kinds of Commonwealth. For the representative must needs be one man, or more; and if more, then it is the assembly of all, or but of a part. When the representative is one man, then is the Commonwealth a monarchy; when an assembly of all that will come together, then it is a democracy, or popular Commonwealth; when an assembly of a part only, then it is called an aristocracy. Other kind of Commonwealth there can be none: for either one, or more, or all, must have the sovereign power (which I have shown to be indivisible) entire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leviathan_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leviathan-19">[18]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autocracy">Autocracy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">Autocracy</a></div>
<p>An autocracy is a system of government in which supreme <a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">power</a> is concentrated in the hands of one person, whose decisions are subject to neither external legal restraints nor regularized mechanisms of popular control (except perhaps for the implicit threat of a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> or mass <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurrection" title="Insurrection">insurrection</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">Absolute monarchy</a> is a historically prevalent form of autocracy, wherein a <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a> governs as a singular <a href="/wiki/Sovereign" title="Sovereign">sovereign</a> with no limitation on <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative" title="Royal prerogative">royal prerogative</a>. Most absolute monarchies are <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary</a>, however some, notably the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">elected</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_college" title="Electoral college">electoral college</a> (such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_cardinals" title="College of cardinals">college of cardinals</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">prince-electors</a>). Other forms of autocracy include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tyranny" title="Tyranny">tyranny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Despotism" title="Despotism">despotism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorship</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aristocracy">Aristocracy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">Aristocracy</a></div>
<p>Aristocracy<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[b]</a></sup> is a form of government that places power in the hands of a small, <a href="/wiki/Elite" title="Elite">elite</a> <a href="/wiki/Ruling_class" title="Ruling class">ruling class</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-OED-22">[20]</a></sup> such as a hereditary <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> or <a href="/wiki/Social_privilege" title="Social privilege">privileged</a> <a href="/wiki/Caste" title="Caste">caste</a>. This class exercises <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minority_rule" title="Minority rule">minority rule</a>, often as a <a href="/wiki/Land_tenure" title="Land tenure">landed</a> <a href="/wiki/Timocracy" title="Timocracy">timocracy</a>, wealthy <a href="/wiki/Plutocracy" title="Plutocracy">plutocracy</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchy</a>.
</p><p>Many monarchies were aristocracies, although in modern constitutional monarchies the monarch may have little effective power. The term <i>aristocracy</i> could also refer to the non-<a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasant</a>, non-servant, and non-<a href="/wiki/Burgher_(social_class)" title="Burgher (social class)">city</a> classes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feudal_system" title="Feudal system">feudal system</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Democracy">Democracy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Democracy_claims.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Democracy_claims.svg/330px-Democracy_claims.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Democracy_claims.svg/495px-Democracy_claims.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Democracy_claims.svg/660px-Democracy_claims.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Democracy_claims.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:green; color:white;"> </span> National governments which self-identify as democracies</div></li><li><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:red; color:black;"> </span> National governments which do not self-identify as democracies</div></li></ul></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electoral_democracies.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1398" data-file-width="2754" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Electoral_democracies.svg/330px-Electoral_democracies.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Electoral_democracies.svg/495px-Electoral_democracies.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Electoral_democracies.svg/660px-Electoral_democracies.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electoral_democracies.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Governments recognised as "electoral democracies" as of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Government&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> by the <i><a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a></i> survey<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[c]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">Democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Types_of_democracy" title="Types of democracy">Types of democracy</a></div>
<p>Democracy is a system of government where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizen" title="Citizen">citizens</a> exercise power by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vote" title="Vote">voting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deliberative_democracy" title="Deliberative democracy">deliberation</a>. In a <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>, the citizenry as a whole directly forms a <a href="/wiki/Participatory_democracy" title="Participatory democracy">participatory</a> governing body and vote directly on each issue. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indirect_democracy" title="Indirect democracy">indirect democracy</a>, the citizenry governs indirectly through the selection of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representatives</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delegated_voting" title="Delegated voting">delegates</a> from among themselves, typically by <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">election</a> or, less commonly, by <a href="/wiki/Sortition" title="Sortition">sortition</a>. These select citizens then meet to form a governing body, such as a legislature or <a href="/wiki/Jury" title="Jury">jury</a>.
</p><p>Some governments combine both direct and indirect democratic governance, wherein the citizenry selects representatives to administer day-to-day governance, while also reserving the right govern directly through <a href="/wiki/Initiative" title="Initiative">popular initiatives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referenda</a> (plebiscites), and the <a href="/wiki/Recall_election" title="Recall election">right of recall</a>. In a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_democracy" title="Constitutional democracy">constitutional democracy</a> the powers of the majority are exercised within the framework of a representative democracy, but the constitution limits <a href="/wiki/Majority_rule" title="Majority rule">majority rule</a>, usually through the provision by all of certain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_right" title="Universal right">universal rights</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_association" title="Freedom of association">freedom of association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-25">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Republics">Republics</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Republic</a></div>
<p>A republic is a form of government in which the country is considered a "public matter" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">res publica</i>), not the private concern or property of the rulers, and where offices of states are subsequently directly or indirectly elected or appointed rather than inherited. The people, or some significant portion of them, have supreme control over the government and where offices of state are elected or chosen by elected people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontesquieu1748book_2,_chapters_1_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontesquieu1748book_2,_chapters_1-26">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-27">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>A common simplified definition of a republic is a government where the head of state is not a monarch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WordNet_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-WordNet-28">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M-W_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-M-W-29">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montesquieu" title="Montesquieu">Montesquieu</a> included both <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracies</a>, where all the people have a share in rule, and <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracies</a> or <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchies</a>, where only some of the people rule, as republican forms of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMontesquieu1748book_2,_chapters_2–3_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontesquieu1748book_2,_chapters_2–3-30">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other terms used to describe different republics include <a href="/wiki/Democratic_republic" title="Democratic republic">democratic republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_republic" title="Semi-presidential republic">semi-presidential republic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_republic" title="Presidential republic">presidential republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_republic" title="People's republic">people's republic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_republic" title="Islamic republic">Islamic republic</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federalism">Federalism</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">Federalism</a></div>
<p>Federalism is a political concept in which a <i>group</i> of members are bound together by <a href="/wiki/Covenant_(law)" title="Covenant (law)">covenant</a> with a governing <a href="/wiki/Federal_headship" title="Federal headship">representative head</a>. The term "federalism" is also used to describe a system of government in which <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> is constitutionally divided between a central governing authority and constituent political units, variously called states, provinces or otherwise. Federalism is a system based upon democratic principles and institutions in which the power to govern is shared between national and provincial/state governments, creating what is often called a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Proponents are often called <a href="/wiki/Federalist" title="Federalist">federalists</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Branches">Branches</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Separation_of_powers.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1086" data-file-width="1504" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Separation_of_powers.png/330px-Separation_of_powers.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Separation_of_powers.png/495px-Separation_of_powers.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Separation_of_powers.png/660px-Separation_of_powers.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Separation_of_powers.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Separation of powers in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_government" title="US government">US government</a>, demonstrating the <i>trias politica</i> model</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">Separation of powers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fusion_of_powers" title="Fusion of powers">Fusion of powers</a></div>
<p>Governments are typically organised into distinct institutions constituting branches of government each with particular <a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">powers</a>, functions, duties, and responsibilities. The distribution of powers between these institutions differs between governments, as do the functions and number of branches. An independent, parallel distribution of powers between branches of government is the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>. A shared, intersecting, or overlapping distribution of powers is the <a href="/wiki/Fusion_of_powers" title="Fusion of powers">fusion of powers</a>.
</p><p>Governments are often organised into three branches with separate powers: a legislature, an executive, and a judiciary; this is sometimes called the <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">trias politica</i></span> model. However, in <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliamentary</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential systems</a>, branches of government often intersect, having shared membership and overlapping functions. Many governments have fewer or additional branches, such as an independent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electoral_commission" title="Electoral commission">electoral commission</a> or <a href="/wiki/Supreme_audit_institution" title="Supreme audit institution">auditory</a> branch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeedler1991[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidFcssj8yigS4CpgPA116_116]–118_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeedler1991[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidFcssj8yigS4CpgPA116_116]–118-31">[28]</a></sup>
</p>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="background:#efefef;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Party_politics" title="Template:Party politics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Party_politics" title="Template talk:Party politics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Party_politics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">Political party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Party_system" title="Party system">Party system</a></div>
<p>Presently, most governments are administered by members of an explicitly constituted <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> which coordinates the activities of associated government <a href="/wiki/Official" title="Official">officials</a> and <a href="/wiki/Candidate" title="Candidate">candidates</a> for office. In a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiparty_system" title="Multiparty system">multiparty system</a> of government, multiple political parties have the capacity to gain control of government offices, typically by competing in <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">elections</a>, although the <a href="/wiki/Effective_number_of_parties" title="Effective number of parties">effective number of parties</a> may be limited.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Majority_government" title="Majority government">majority government</a> is a government by one or more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governing_party" title="Governing party">governing parties</a> together holding an absolute majority of seats in the parliament, in contrast to a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority government</a> in which they have only a plurality of seats and often depend on a <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">confidence and supply</a> arrangement with other parties. A <a href="/wiki/Coalition_government" title="Coalition government">coalition government</a> is one in which multiple parties cooperate to form a government as part of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coalition_agreement" title="Coalition agreement">coalition agreement</a>. In a single-party government a single party forms a government without the support of a coalition, as is typically the case with majority governments,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGallagherLaverMair2006_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGallagherLaverMair2006-32">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKettle2015_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKettle2015-33">[30]</a></sup> but even a minority government may consist of just one party unable to find a willing coalition partner at the moment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDuxbury2021_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDuxbury2021-34">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>A party which continuously maintains a single-party government within a (nominally) multiparty system constitutes a <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant-party system</a>. In a (nondemocratic) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_party_system" title="One party system">one party system</a> a single <a href="/wiki/Ruling_party" title="Ruling party">ruling party</a> has the (more or less) exclusive right to form the government, and the formation of other parties may be obstructed or illegal. In some cases, a government may have a <a href="/wiki/Nonpartisanism" title="Nonpartisanism">non-partisan system</a>, as is the case with <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Non-partisan_democracy" title="Non-partisan democracy">non-partisan democracy</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maps">Maps</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_system_of_government" title="List of countries by system of government">List of countries by system of government</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:612px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1314" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg/610px-EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg/915px-EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg/1220px-EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg.png 2x" width="610"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EIU_Democracy_Index_2017.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> <hr/> <div> <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"> <tbody><tr> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <b>Full Democracies</b> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#006837; color:white;"> </span> 9–10</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#1a9850; color:black;"> </span> 8–9</div> </td> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <b>Flawed Democracies</b> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#66bd63; color:black;"> </span> 7–8</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#a6d96a; color:black;"> </span> 5–6</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#fdae61; <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFFrederickson2000">Frederickson 2000</a>, p. 12, quote:"...conservative southern Democrats viewed warily the potential of New Deal programs to threaten the region's economic dependence on cheap labor while stirring the democratic ambitions of the disfranchised and undermining white supremacy."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">ἀριστοκρατία</span> <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn">aristokratía</i></span>, from <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">ἄριστος</span></span> <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aristocrat#English" title="wikt:aristocrat">aristos</a></i></span> "excellent", and <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">κράτος</span></span> <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language romanization"><i lang="grc-Latn"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/kratos" title="wikt:kratos">kratos</a></i></span> "<a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">power</a>".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Conducted by American <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a> <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>, which is largely funded by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_government" title="US government">US government</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
